However, there have been records of very worn female Greater Scaup in the SW. ----After reviewing photos and head shape, appears to be more in line with GRSC. The bill shape is broader and flatter than LESC and the white patch at the base is larger than compared to LESC. Photos on checklist from 31 JUL from other observer also shows better the rounded head shape when bird is in water. Finally, I learned that female GRSC can have a pale auricular patch in Spring and Summer while in LESC  this feature is rarer. This can be seen in my photos. Based on head shape, bill size, white patch at base of bill, and auricular patch,  I changed my observation to GRSC.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS1072664584	2021-02-13 15:56:58.405597	596	species	Greater Scaup	Aythya marila			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Clark	US-NV-003		33			Cornerstone Park	L2753168	H	36.0369429	-115.0544178	2021-02-13	07:00:00	obsr1472242	S81215024	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	245	3.219		2	1		0	1	0			I studied this individual for approximately 45 minutes from 30 ft away. Being familiar and experienced with the challenges of differentiating Lesser from Greater, I was pretty surprised after carefully scrutinizing this specimen to draw a confident conclusion of Greater Scaup. I examined the bird from 10-15 different angles and from various lighting/shading scenarios. Never really expected something like this on Cornerstone Lake. Lesser would certainly be the most expected hands down. Luckily, the bird is extremely cooperative and almost "approachable" so to speak, offering detailed study. It should also be noted - at one point a harrier came in and got all the waterfowl up on the wing. While flying, this bird CLEARLY had "white" extending from the secondaries very noticeably out through the primaries on the trailing edge of the wing. Combined with other field marks related to head shape, and the amount of black on the bill tip, this bird is "solid" for Greater Scaup. Though the bird is also showing a very noticeable green gloss to the head (as is usually pointed out as a field mark for Greater in nearly every FG), this is an unreliable trait to use, as just the angle of the sun on the individuals head can change that green gloss to a variety of colors, thus potentially confusing or leading to incorrect ID for those with less experience with the complexities of scaup identification.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS505814376	2018-08-04 09:52:54	596	species	Greater Scaup	Aythya marila			4				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Elko	US-NV-007	US-NV_947	9	USFWS_518		Ruby Lake NWR - (40.2020,-115.4931)	L5901117	P	40.2020330	-115.4930780	2017-05-28	10:12:00	obsr20114	S37225373	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	150	8.047		13	1		0	1	1			These birds were in the large flock of multi species ducks including Lesser Scaups. We eliminated all species of ducks except for the Scaups and the Ring-necked because of their white flakes and sides and their dark heads, breasts and the rear of the body. --The Ring-necked Duck was eliminated because the birds in question did not have rings on their bills and there was no spike of white behind the breast. --None of the Scaups were diving, therefore we were able to determine the shape of the head with a fair degree of accuracy. The heads were relatively blocky in shape in sloped slightly toward the rear. In fact, they were almost rectangular with rounds corners. Whereas the Lessers head is narrower from front to back and looks peaked. The bills when seen from the side we're very deep or thick at the base and were about twice as deep as the distance from the top of the bill to the top of the forehead. That same field mark on Lester Scaup would show a forehead height of about twice the depth of the bill. Two of the birds flew and that clinched the species because the inner primaries where off-white. The Lessers inner primary are dark.
